<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1386401708">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386401708" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/39981962-amanda-orneck" class="left imgcol" title="Amanda Orneck"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442965393p2/39981962.jpg" alt="Amanda Orneck" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1386401708?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/39981962-amanda-orneck" class="user" title="Amanda Orneck">Amanda Orneck</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8177268-night-mare" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1386401708">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3806670066094715419">Frustrating though imaginative, mean-spirited and misogynistic, an example of how not to portray women in fiction. It saddens me to say that this will be the last Xanth novel I read for the forseeable future. Once I slogged through Night Mare I no longer wanted to spend time with this writer, and it’s for the strangest reason: This book, featuring a female protagonist destined to save her kingdom from ultimate destruction, is just a diatribe against women.<br /><br />Imbri is a former Night Mare, a horse th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3806670066094715419">Frustrating though imaginative, mean-spirited and misogynistic, an example of how not to portray women in fiction. It saddens me to say that this will be the last Xanth novel I read for the forseeable future. Once I slogged through Night Mare I no longer wanted to spend time with this writer, and it’s for the strangest reason: This book, featuring a female protagonist destined to save her kingdom from ultimate destruction, is just a diatribe against women.<br /><br />Imbri is a former Night Mare, a horse that brings bad dreams to all the people in Xanth. After the events of Ogre, Ogre she is no longer able to do her job properly, and so she’s fired and sent to help stave off the next major invasion threatening Xanth. Not only is a barbaric army cutting a swath down through Xanth toward the seat of power, someone is also magically taking out the kings of the nation, and no one can figure out why.<br /><br />Where Ogre, Ogre represents the best of Piers Anthony, the next book in the series manages to be his worst. Imbri and her companions are constantly demeaned, and usually it’s the women themselves that are constantly talking about the weaknesses of their gender. Over and over again the women in this book opine that they don’t really want to be valued members of society, they just want to be longed for by their men, that their intelligence is the ugliest trait, and that they should use their bodies as bait for the enemy. This misogyny culminates in a climax scene where a character must conquer her own weak feminine biology in order to prevail against her enemy. <br /><br />I wish I could recommend skipping this book, but Fantasy readers tend to be completionists, and that requires reading even the horrible entries in a series. For me, it’s going to take a long time before I will be able to get back to Xanth. Let’s just say, I’ll need to spend some time away from the Gap Chasm in order to forget it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3806670066094715419">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_597703912">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/597703912" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/84660-swankivy" class="left imgcol" title="Swankivy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1220079335p2/84660.jpg" alt="Swankivy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/597703912?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 22, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/84660-swankivy" class="user" title="Swankivy">Swankivy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15433.Night_Mare" title="paperback 9780345418548" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer597703912">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5364403581920829378">Imbrium is the main character of this story. She's the author's first female protagonist in this series, and though she is a horse (a night mare to be exact), she's still handled with the same sort of disrespect that Anthony frequently frames his female characters. At one point she is made powerless because a man tricks her into being dominated by him (he gets on her back and fits her with a bit, and she can't escape), and later the same man turns out to be a shapeshifter who dominates her by sh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5364403581920829378">Imbrium is the main character of this story. She's the author's first female protagonist in this series, and though she is a horse (a night mare to be exact), she's still handled with the same sort of disrespect that Anthony frequently frames his female characters. At one point she is made powerless because a man tricks her into being dominated by him (he gets on her back and fits her with a bit, and she can't escape), and later the same man turns out to be a shapeshifter who dominates her by shifting into his horse form while she's "in season." Convenient, no, that the female's one weakness is her complete inability to resist the sexy man? Her urges overcome her and she's done in by her own attraction! This is the kind of thing that makes a lot of these books sound like a disturbing boy fantasy. That stuff can really be dangerous. But I'll look at the story too.<br /><br />It's pretty inventive, though transparent in places. I still like the "gourd" world--the dream underground of sorts where nightmares come from. It was very clear that the man wearing a gold band was the same person as the horse wearing it, so I don't know what Anthony was trying to pull with that revelation. I also thought the succession of kings was interesting . . . the existing king was in an apparently hypnotic state and couldn't rule any more, so the successor got on the throne, and one by one their consciousnesses were captured by the Horseman. The rule was that Xanth could only be ruled by a Magician-class talented person. And when they start running out of possible kings, oh dearie me, it strikes them to wonder . . . hey, maybe we could get chicks to do it! Girl kings! No one ever thought of that before, even though the definitive factor for eligibility was supposed to be their magical strength. The very fact that anyone had to consider this a revelation is pretty telling. But for some reason, especially when I was a kid, I found it engaging to find out who'd be the next king to lead Xanth through an influx of attacks from Mundania while fearing being the next to be captured.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5364403581920829378">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1006241671?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 25, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/24009998-julie-decker" class="user" title="Julie Decker">Julie Decker</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1006241671">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16271851038507319803">Imbrium is a Night Mare who, like many in her land, gets charmed by the Horseman while investigating the rash of kidnapped Xanthian kings. As more and more of Xanth's royalty are getting transported to a hypnotic state, the next successor must take the throne, and it may be up to Imbrium to break the chain.<br /><br />This was the only <em>Xanth</em> book that I liked as much as the first one. Mostly because the ideas in the "gourd" world invention were pretty fresh and unique. What I didn't like so much was (again)</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16271851038507319803">Imbrium is a Night Mare who, like many in her land, gets charmed by the Horseman while investigating the rash of kidnapped Xanthian kings. As more and more of Xanth's royalty are getting transported to a hypnotic state, the next successor must take the throne, and it may be up to Imbrium to break the chain.<br /><br />This was the only <em>Xanth</em> book that I liked as much as the first one. Mostly because the ideas in the "gourd" world invention were pretty fresh and unique. What I didn't like so much was (again) how ladies were handled here. Imbrium is the author's first female protagonist, though she is a horse. Her big downfall is that she cannot resist the sexiness of a male horse and her weakness overcomes her. And also, though having Magician-class magic is the only requirement of a Xanth King, they apparently have never considered crowning a woman before (unless it's through marriage to a male king), so having to use female kings in a pinch when they ran out of men was pitched as clever. I thought it should have been obvious.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer994928795">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6125691866857715815">I liked the book, but had trouble getting into the first half of the story. It probably deserves 3 1/2 stars instead of the three I gave it.<br /><br />For those who read Ogre, Ogre, you will find some of the same characters appear in this story, including the main character, Mare Imbrie. Still carrying a half of a soul, Imbrie has not been doing well as a Night Mare. She has trouble being as sinister as she needs to be, and even dreams of seeing the rainbow. The Night Stallion sends her out into the day, w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6125691866857715815">I liked the book, but had trouble getting into the first half of the story. It probably deserves 3 1/2 stars instead of the three I gave it.<br /><br />For those who read Ogre, Ogre, you will find some of the same characters appear in this story, including the main character, Mare Imbrie. Still carrying a half of a soul, Imbrie has not been doing well as a Night Mare. She has trouble being as sinister as she needs to be, and even dreams of seeing the rainbow. The Night Stallion sends her out into the day, with a warning to King Trent to "Beware the horseman!" However, King Trent becomes enchanted. The Kingship falls to Prince Dor, until the pattern repeats itself. While Xanth is losing King after King to some sort of enchantment, the Nextwave is progressing across the land. Imbrie even becomes captured by the nefarious Horseman, only to find out how cruel Mundanes can be. As time passes, it become apparent that the future fate of Xanth is dependent upon this Night Mare.<br /><br />Fans of the series should enjoy this book. Older characters such as Bink, Chameleon, King Trent and Queen Iris make an appearance, while sharing space with the second generation characters such as Dor, Irene, Chet, Chem, Tandy and Smash. And it is the story of Night Mare Imbrie that brings this cast of characters together.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_667883338">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667883338" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1938544-michael" class="left imgcol" title="Michael"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1330120106p2/1938544.jpg" alt="Michael" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/667883338?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 14, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1938544-michael" class="user" title="Michael">Michael</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15537.Night_Mare" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345304568" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">young adults, ya fans, fantasy fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Michael by: </span>
      Seth Klein
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1938544-michael?shelf=satire" class="actionLinkLite">satire</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1938544-michael?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer667883338">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9363573712767884606">For some reason, this is the only one of my Xanth books which I have kept since my own early adulthood, when I devoured all of them (8 of them, I think, at the time) in a remarkably short time and then lost all interest before the next one had come out. This is the sixth in the series, and it certainly wasn’t the best. I may have held on to it because of the extensive use of the nightmare world of the “gourds,” but I suspect that it was just the luck that in this case the cover never fell off.<br /><br />At</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9363573712767884606">For some reason, this is the only one of my Xanth books which I have kept since my own early adulthood, when I devoured all of them (8 of them, I think, at the time) in a remarkably short time and then lost all interest before the next one had come out. This is the sixth in the series, and it certainly wasn’t the best. I may have held on to it because of the extensive use of the nightmare world of the “gourds,” but I suspect that it was just the luck that in this case the cover never fell off.<br /><br />At the time I first read, I probably would have given it three or four stars. I re-read it more recently during a period of sadness, because I wanted something simple and familiar, and even for that purpose it was a bit too silly. It’s written for a childlike audience, and in order to get anything out of it, you still have to be pretty childish. The story centers on a magic horse whose job is to deliver horrific images to day-dwelling creatures, but who has been granted a soul and is finding her work increasingly difficult due to empathy. She finds herself caught up in an invasion of the magical realm of Xanth by “mundanes” from our world who hope to conquer and destroy. The mundanes have a secret weapon that eliminates each new King of Xanth in succession, leaving it without leadership in its time of need. <br /><br />In all, the writing is competent enough, and I enjoyed all the puns when I was a kid, but this really isn’t my sort of thing anymore.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_253516813">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253516813" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies" class="left imgcol" title="David Sarkies"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1445680853p2/5856247.jpg" alt="David Sarkies" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/253516813?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 04, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies" class="user" title="David Sarkies">David Sarkies</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15433.Night_Mare" title="paperback 9780345418548" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tweens who liked the Harry Potter Books</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to David by: </span>
      Stewart Wymer
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer253516813">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2385021305162755195"><strong>A nightmare is actually a mythological creature</strong><br />30 December 2011<br /><br /> Well, at this point in the Xanth series we are starting to move away from the main characters from the previous books to single books, set in Xanth, evolving around a new character. In this novel we meet Mare Imbrium, a Night Mare. Nightmares are given the task of carrying bad dreams to the people of Xanth. However Imbrium's problem is that she has obtained half a soul (which she got from the previous book) and this has affected her</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2385021305162755195"><strong>A nightmare is actually a mythological creature</strong><br />30 December 2011<br /><br />	Well, at this point in the Xanth series we are starting to move away from the main characters from the previous books to single books, set in Xanth, evolving around a new character. In this novel we meet Mare Imbrium, a Night Mare. Nightmares are given the task of carrying bad dreams to the people of Xanth. However Imbrium's problem is that she has obtained half a soul (which she got from the previous book) and this has affected her ability to carry out her task.	<br />	Piers Anthony does like playing with words, but then he was not the first person to connect nightmares with horses. I have seen this a while back in the worlds of Dungeons and Dragons, where nightmares are from the nether regions, and are dark demonic horses that travel on paths of fire. However Anthony's nightmare is a little tamer than the nastier creatures that appear in Dungeons of Dragons. However, a little research has revealed that nightmares have been connected with horses long before the development of Dungeons and Dragons, and in fact are <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mare_%28folklore%29">demonic creatures</a> in German folklore (as is evident by this painting, so it seems that Anthony's pun has backfired):<br /><br /><img width="325" height="263" class="escapedImg" alt="John Henry Fusali – The Nightmare" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379757452i/174260._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />	The other thing that I immediately noticed after reading the outline of the book, and that is the name of the nightmare. Mare Imbrium: that is the name of a region of the <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mare_Imbrium">lunar surface</a> which, for some strange reason, are called seas (even though there is no water in them – Mare is a Latin word that refers to a large body of water). I would have never picked that up when I originally read the book, however it has since jumped out at me from my computer screen upon noticing it this time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2385021305162755195">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_185769833">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185769833" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4514937-the-joy-of-booking" class="left imgcol" title="The Joy of Booking"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1326859742p2/4514937.jpg" alt="The Joy of Booking" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/185769833?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 17, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4514937-the-joy-of-booking" class="user" title="The Joy of Booking">The Joy of Booking</a>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer185769833">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13165765410421655220">Night Mare (and the rest of the Xanth series) sadly didn't hold up to a re-reading as an adult, but as a pre-teen and young teenager, I found these hilarious and wonderful.<br /><br />Piers Anthony specializes in a kind of subversive and dirty humor that's just on this side of not appropriate for children. They're also almost terrifying, in a way that left me wanting more. That combined with the mythology made for absorbing childhood reading for me.<br /><br />The one thing that saved the book upon my adult re-read was</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13165765410421655220">Night Mare (and the rest of the Xanth series) sadly didn't hold up to a re-reading as an adult, but as a pre-teen and young teenager, I found these hilarious and wonderful.<br /><br />Piers Anthony specializes in a kind of subversive and dirty humor that's just on this side of not appropriate for children. They're also almost terrifying, in a way that left me wanting more. That combined with the mythology made for absorbing childhood reading for me.<br /><br />The one thing that saved the book upon my adult re-read was the amazingly intricate world that Anthony has created for Xanth. Located on what we Mundanians consider to be the state of Florida, Xanth is really a magical world populated by gorgons, fairies, trolls and all manner of fantastical creatures. (The Night Mares of this tale are working horses who deliver scary dreams to the inhabitants of the mundane world, named after the lakes of the moon.) In addition to creating exactly the sort of fantasy world I love, Anthony also makes genius word play involving a lot of literalism and in-jokes, which make for reading the entire series multiple times a lot of fun when you're twelve.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13165765410421655220">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/519749752" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6436072-sam-lackey" class="left imgcol" title="Sam Lackey"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1316913310p2/6436072.jpg" alt="Sam Lackey" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/519749752?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6436072-sam-lackey" class="user" title="Sam Lackey">Sam Lackey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15433.Night_Mare" title="paperback 9780345418548" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer519749752">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12067490072452630475">Night Mare reads like a lazy attempt to revisit all of the characters from the previous novels in the Xanth series. It will be the last Xanth book that I read, and probably the last Piers Anthony book that I read.<br /><br />While younger readers might appreciate the childish humor, mainly in the form of puns and wordplay, Night Mare-- like almost all of the other Xanth novels, offers nothing for someone wanting to delve into a good fantasy novel. <br /><br />There really isn't anything redeeming for younger readers, e</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12067490072452630475">Night Mare reads like a lazy attempt to revisit all of the characters from the previous novels in the Xanth series. It will be the last Xanth book that I read, and probably the last Piers Anthony book that I read.<br /><br />While younger readers might appreciate the childish humor, mainly in the form of puns and wordplay, Night Mare-- like almost all of the other Xanth novels, offers nothing for someone wanting to delve into a good fantasy novel. <br /><br />There really isn't anything redeeming for younger readers, either. Women and girls exist in the world of Xanth as sexual objects. Though, in Night Mare, a few women finally take part in battle and take the throne, it is only a few pages of the story before the girls fall. Anthony's characters take a lot about the roles of girls. Nymphs are used in battle to lure away the invading army. <br /><br />Even the hero of Night Mare, a horse whose previous job was to deliver bad dreams, cannot resist the antagonist when he is in horse form. One character's magical ability is sex appeal. Another character's magical ability is to become more attractive, but less intelligent (while becoming later more ugly but smart). <br /><br />I could go on about what Night Mare fails to do, but it really isn't worth it. Skip this book, and skip all Xanth books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12067490072452630475">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_386368499">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/386368499" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11455886-j-austill" class="left imgcol" title="J Austill"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1369205964p2/11455886.jpg" alt="J Austill" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/386368499?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 21, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11455886-j-austill" class="user" title="J Austill">J Austill</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15433.Night_Mare" title="paperback 9780345418548" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer386368499">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3895388261914883493">This, the 6th Xanth book, is sort of hit or miss for me. On one hand, it is the first time that we get a female protagonist and it turns out that Piers does just fine writing for the opposite sex. It also continues the new trend from the last book of having a non-human protagonist. She's a horse. Well, more correctly a night mare which is a horse which delivers dreams. Imbrium has found herself changed from the other night mares after gaining part of a soul at the end of the previous book and as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3895388261914883493">This, the 6th Xanth book, is sort of hit or miss for me. On one hand, it is the first time that we get a female protagonist and it turns out that Piers does just fine writing for the opposite sex. It also continues the new trend from the last book of having a non-human protagonist. She's a horse. Well, more correctly a night mare which is a horse which delivers dreams. Imbrium has found herself changed from the other night mares after gaining part of a soul at the end of the previous book and as such has to go off on her own quest to discover her true love and place in life.<br /><br />This book does establish a few of the rules of Xanth, which I mentioned previously in my A Spell for Chameleon review. This makes Night Mare a must read in the Xanth series. <br /><br />The rules of Xanth:<br /><br />1. Xanth is a magical world which exists in parallel to our own. Everyone born in Xanth (human or otherwise) is born with a magical talent.<br />2. Each magical talent is different and none is duplicated though they can be similar.<br />3. Not all talents are equal. The most powerful talents are considered Magician (or Sorceress) caliber. <br />4. The King of Xanth is the person who has the most powerful talent, as this allows them to protect their subjects. This fact disregards gender. The Queen of Xanth is the person who is married to the king. <br />5. Any person who does not have a magical talent was not born in Xanth (see rule 1) and is therefore exiled from Xanth (to prevent illegal immigration).<br /><br />In particular, this book sets up the rules for ascension to ruler. The plot of the book being that some unknown person wants to eliminate the government of Xanth by incapacitating the King. We then find out the order of ascension to the throne and who can qualify for that job. <br /><br />But here is where we have the major flaw of the book. After establishing who are the magician level persons in Xanth and what order they will ascend to the thrown, the author seems to get a bit bored with it. We have to trudge through the list with each having some turn at the throne. Only once the sequence is complete does the plot continue and resolve. It seems to me that once the sequence has been set up, it does not necessarily have to go through to conclusion, we can move on. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3895388261914883493">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The message, "Beware the Horseman," is not understood and the focus turns to the invading Mundanes, called the Nextwave. King Trint, along with each successor is caught up in a sightless open eyed stare. After the ruling men of the land fall victim to the sorcerous powers of a hidden enemy, Imbri the night mare becomes the unlikely hero as she and the other women of Xanth must rally the forces of magic and might against the brutal, invading Mundane army. Chock full of cameos by characters from every previous adventure, this entry builds on the magical world of Xanth that has been vividly illustrated by Anthony and enthralls</span>

Chock full of cameos by characters from every previous adventure, this entry builds on the magical world of Xanth that has been vividly illustrated by Anthony and enthralls the reader with the greatest peril they have ever faced.</span>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gcScW6vP9h5rBR3FDKDMW8bWxB2SrEHvNuPXOkIYpdHkEKOIWR3i5OfdaX5ywSrpjyEHBNtxBkVc6tKojo1TlA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MGZymOhc58mLkkYJGnOIYuCRaZc9XMQNILu9XV31SCdVsk1LGo7zMwdKMrJkEm7QqWaqjnSBg6dKsrjPkWC+Yg==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8516.Piers_Anthony">About Piers Anthony</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/8516.Piers_Anthony"><img alt="8516" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1445445112p2/8516.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7066908662256507670">Though he spent the first four years of his life in England, Piers never returned to live in his country of birth after moving to Spain and immigrated to America at age six. After graduating with a B.A. from Goddard College, he married one of his fellow students and and spent fifteen years in an assortment of professions before he began writing fiction full-time.<br /><br />Piers is a self-proclaimed environm</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7066908662256507670">Though he spent the first four years of his life in England, Piers never returned to live in his country of birth after moving to Spain and immigrated to America at age six. After graduating with a B.A. from Goddard College, he married one of his fellow students and and spent fifteen years in an assortment of professions before he began writing fiction full-time.<br /><br />Piers is a self-proclaimed environmentalist and lives on a tree farm in Florida with his wife. They have two grown daughters.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/piersanthony" target="_blank">http://us.macmillan.com/author/piersa...</a></span>
